---
title: "Help!! White screen, black screen but no fglrx..."
date: 2007-10-25
forum: Multimedia &amp; Video
---

### Post by LeBurt on 2007-10-25
I've been trying and trying and some more since Gutsy was out and I'm still not an inch ahead of where I was. It appears I'm hitting every problem in the book installing drivers for my Radeon All-In-Wonder 9600 (RV350 GPU). I have however tried to document my problems as best I can. Help would be greatly appreciated!!

Problem: I cannot get ATI's fglrx driver to work.

Symptom: Upon booting, I get a white screen using the default "ati" driver, and a black screen using "fglrx". From there, I get no response whatsoever from anything. My only option out is a hard reset.

System details:
a) using an ACER AL2216W LCD display, native resolution 1680x1050
b) my CPU is AMD 64 3000+
c) Gutsy is the i386 32-bit version, stock
d) Graphic card is ATI All-in-Wonder 9600 series (RV350 GPU I believe)

What I did so far:

1. Fresh Gutsy install, all booted ok using "ati" device in xorg.conf

2. Followed procedure of [this thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=575843") using the new 8.42.3 driver, went up to step 7 and rebooted as suggested. I was able to log in normally and then, whitescreen! In fact, I can see my Desktop for a very short time before everything turns white. Below are xorg.conf and Xorg.0.log for this attempt. Interesting detail: mouse cursor is still visible and alive...

xorg.conf:

I haven't seen enough of those yet but it doesn't seem like it's ending properly.

5. While I was in recovery mode, I switched back to the original (ati) xorg.conf file and rebooted. Got to the same white screen as above.

6. I hit [CTRL][ALT][F1] again and switched to the second (fglrx) xorg.conf file. I went back to X and hit [CTRL][ALT][Backspace] to restart it. This time, everything booted ok. The xorg log below:

### Post by renzokuken on 2007-10-25
looks to me like the fglrx driver hasnt installed properly. have a look in the forums and in launchpad for the "mesa issue"

EDIT:  have a look here [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=569654](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=569654) particularly michael37's post (about 5th/6th one down), in the trouble shooting section

---

### Post by xocekim on 2007-10-25
I had the same problem. I went into CTRL + ALT + F1 and edited xorg.conf adding this
```
Section "Extensions"
	Option	    "Composite" "0"
EndSection
```

Then CTRL + ALT + F7 and I could then login ok and fglrx driver was working as it should. To get Compiz to work I edit xorg.conf again, this time turning the Composite extension back on
```
Section "Extensions"
	Option	    "Composite" "1"
EndSection
```

CTRL + ALT + BACKSPACE

All working, I have to do this each time I reboot though :(

---

### Post by LeBurt on 2007-10-25
I resolved the black screen problem!!

Found the answer [here]("http://wiki.cchtml.com/index.php/Ubuntu_Dapper_Installation_Guide").

First, since I was having this error in Xorg.0.log:
(WW) fglrx(0): Failed to load DRM connection

I did:
```
depmod -ae
```

Then, because I had the black screen with the fglrx driver, I added this line in xorg.conf, in the device section containing "fglrx":

```
Option "BusType" "PCI"
```

I'm able to start normally now, although I'm not sure which of the above actually fixed the problem.

So now, I'm left with the MESA problem as with a lot of people. I haven't done much research there yet but I'll post my answer here when I find a solution.

```
burt@Desktopita-L:~$ fglrxinfo
display: :0.0  screen: 0
OpenGL vendor string: Mesa project: www.mesa3d.org
OpenGL renderer string: Mesa GLX Indirect
OpenGL version string: 1.4 (2.1 Mesa 7.0.1)
```

### Post by LeBurt on 2007-10-26
Now this is interesting,,,

Before investigating the mesa problem (which is still there), I thought I'd see if compiz would initialize so went ahead and applied [this procedure]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=588428"):

Added in xorg.conf:
```
Section "Extensions"
        Option "Composite" "1"
EndSection

Section "ServerFlags"
        Option "AIGLX" "on"
EndSection

```

Modified /etc/xdg/compiz/compiz-manager to include this:
```
WHITELIST="nvidia intel ati radeon i810 fglrx"
```

### Post by xocekim on 2007-10-26
After booting up today I investigated a bit more and found this to be the source of my whitescreen and Mesa driver problem.

```
sudo ln -sf /lib/modules/$(uname -r)/misc/fglrx.ko /lib/modules/$(uname -r)/volatile/fglrx.ko
```

Then CTRL + ALT + BACKSPACE and fglrx driver kicks in and all is well, give it a try. Got it from [this guide]("http://wiki.cchtml.com/index.php/Ubuntu_Gutsy_Installation_Guide").

---

### Post by LeBurt on 2007-10-27
Thinking aloud here so I can keep track of what I'm doing.

1. Been exploring /var/log/Xorg.0.log in more detail and found this:
(II) fglrx(0): AGP card detected
(**) fglrx(0): Forced into PCI mode

Just wondering if that second line could be because I added this in xorg.conf:
Option "BusType" "PCI"  ?

Whenever I remove that line from xorg.conf, I get the black screen lock-up described earlier. 

Therefore:
a) could it be that my ATI card works fine in "PCI mode" but not in some "AGP mode"?
b) this would lead me to conclude that the problem is not with the card itself but with AGP in my system!! I've an AMD Athlon 64 3000+ with a SiS760 chipset...
c) could it be that the "PCI mode" prevents DRI from initializing properly?

2. Continuing on the AGP topic:
```
burt@Desktopita-L:$ lsmod | grep agp
amd64_agp              13700  0 
sis_agp                10116  1 
agpgart                35016  3 fglrx,amd64_agp,sis_agp

```

There is a sis_agp AND and amd64_agp module in there, does that look normal? 

Just for the sake of it, I blindly tried blacklisting the amd64_agp module by adding this to /etc/modprobe.d/blacklist:
```
blacklist amd64_agp
```

Everything worked as normal but the module did indeed disappear from lsmod.

Therefore:
a) how do I move ahead with this?
b) how does one troubleshoot *potential* AGP problems?

3) By looking at this from Xorg.0.log:
```
(EE) fglrx(0): atiddxDriScreenInit failed, GPS not been initialized. 
(WW) fglrx(0): ***********************************************
(WW) fglrx(0): * DRI initialization failed!                  *
(WW) fglrx(0): * (maybe driver kernel module missing or bad) *
(WW) fglrx(0): * 2D acceleraton available (MMIO)             *
(WW) fglrx(0): * no 3D acceleration available                *
(WW) fglrx(0): ********************************************* *

```

a) What can we conclude about the first line, that atiddxDriScreenInit failed?
b) What is GPS and is the fact that it didn't initialize the cause of "atiddxDriScreenInit failed" ?
c) Are the mesa and DRI problems linked? Which one comes first?
